  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1f300779-0941-4574-8ea4-68612c6994b4'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer2065620193520710704">Sixteen when a baby is brought to her to raise, Sybel has grown up on Eld Mountain. Her only playmates are the creatures of a fantastic menagerie called there by wizardry. Sybel has cared nothing for humans, until the baby awakens emotions previously unknown to her. And when Coren--the man who brought this child--returns, Sybel's world is again turned upside down.<br/></span>

<div id="review_1619895170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1619895170" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1619895170?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575077652" href="/book/show/1681934.The_Forgotten_Beasts_of_Eld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=romantica">romantica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=z-patricia-a-mckillip">z-patricia-a-mckillip</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=alpha-team">alpha-team</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=fantasy-60s-70s-80s">fantasy-60s-70s-80s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1619895170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13089682408332791236">how to express how much I love Patricia McKillip and her books, how much her stories move me, how they slowly and invisibly transform from enthralling fairy tale to a genuinely emotional experience? how to describe the prose: so refined and elegant, so expressive, so light and delicate, so deep and beautiful, and yet often so simple? just so: her arrangements are perfect, my own kind of perfect. how to describe all of that, to make into something as plodding as a book review? love is a subjectiv</span>
  <span id="freeText13089682408332791236" style="display:none">how to express how much I love Patricia McKillip and her books, how much her stories move me, how they slowly and invisibly transform from enthralling fairy tale to a genuinely emotional experience? how to describe the prose: so refined and elegant, so expressive, so light and delicate, so deep and beautiful, and yet often so simple? just so: her arrangements are perfect, my own kind of perfect. how to describe all of that, to make into something as plodding as a book review? love is a subjective experience and so resists codification. it would be easier to describe why I liked that walk in a forest, that beam of sunlight hitting the leaves in just that way; or how I like to watch the fog roll in past that great hill, making of the world a dreamscape. words seems so small for such a task, and yet words are the very tools she uses.<br /><br />the tale is about a magical woman in a forest. she is a cold woman and her forest is surrounded by an angry world. she surrounds herself in turn, with what she loves, the only things she truly understands: her beasts - her friends. the story is about being loved and falling in love; it is about making bad decisions and letting terrible things turn you into something terrible. it is about being understood and not being understood, why understanding is not always necessary, why it can be hardest to understand yourself. it is about letting go; it is about letting other people be a part of you. it is a fable, and so much more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13089682408332791236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_826496826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826496826" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826496826?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=comfort-read">comfort-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=animalia">animalia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=here-there-be-dragons">here-there-be-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826496826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17722396125306034198"><i>The Forgotten Beasts of Eld</i> is one of my all-time favorite fantasy novels. It's a total comfort read, poetry in prose combined with an appealing story, some great symbolism, and an examination of people and their motives and how our desires and fears can make or undo us. It's one of the fantasy books I repeatedly recommend to friends.<br/><br/> I finished this off yesterday in one day, as part of a buddy read with the Buddies, Books and Baubles group. It's probably my third or fourth read of it, but it's </span>
  <span id="freeText17722396125306034198" style="display:none"><i>The Forgotten Beasts of Eld</i> is one of my all-time favorite fantasy novels. It's a total comfort read, poetry in prose combined with an appealing story, some great symbolism, and an examination of people and their motives and how our desires and fears can make or undo us. It's one of the fantasy books I repeatedly recommend to friends.<br /><br /> I finished this off yesterday in one day, as part of a buddy read with the Buddies, Books and Baubles group. It's probably my third or fourth read of it, but it's been ages since I last read it, so there were quite a few details that I'd forgotten. I still love it as much as ever, though.<br /><br />Sybel is a young woman who's a powerful wizard. Raised in isolation by her father on Eld Mountain and orphaned at age 16, she's inherited a marvelous menagerie of powerful and wise magical animals. When a young lord, Coren, brings her a baby, Tamlorn, a pawn in the power plays of men, and begs her to raise and protect him, she somewhat reluctantly agrees. But twelve years later, Coren asks for Tamlorn back ... and then Tamlorn's father, King Drede, appears at Sybel's door. And Sybel finds herself very unwillingly drawn into their world.<br /><br />**slightly spoilerish discussion of symbols in the rest of this review**<br /><br />Thoughts on symbolism: Rommalb/Blammor, of course, is fear - that's made quite explicit. I've always thought the Liralen was a pretty clear symbol of love, but I did a little spot-checking of online reviews and saw some other people suggest that it's happiness or joy. That would make some sense, but I still think love is the better answer. For one thing, when Sybel calls the Liralen, she usually is subconsciously calling Coren. <br /><br />It's an interesting idea, though, the juxtaposition of fear with love (or happiness) as flip sides to the same magical creature.<br /><br />A beautiful book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17722396125306034198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2039503895" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2039503895" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Evgeny by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/55066255-a-dawes">A. Dawes</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2039503895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer900356290223739797">A guy was born in a remote village who could talk to animals and call them to him. He build himself a hermit hut and called some exotic and legendary animals, including a ballad-singing boar (my imagination miserably fails at trying to imaging it in the act), <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532915204i/26048728._SX540_.jpg' alt='Singing boar' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>and of cause a treasure-hoarding dragon. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532915364i/26048745._SX540_.jpg' alt='Dragon' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>His son continued his father collection, but his only heir was a girl named Sybel - a heroine of the story. As much as she was trying to avoid any interaction with other humans, the Big Politics caug</span>
  <span id="freeText900356290223739797" style="display:none">A guy was born in a remote village who could talk to animals and call them to him. He build himself a hermit hut and called some exotic and legendary animals, including a ballad-singing boar (my imagination miserably fails at trying to imaging it in the act), <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532915204i/26048728._SX540_.jpg" alt="Singing boar" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and of cause a treasure-hoarding dragon. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532915364i/26048745._SX540_.jpg" alt="Dragon" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>His son continued his father collection, but his only heir was a girl named Sybel - a heroine of the story. As much as she was trying to avoid any interaction with other humans, the Big Politics caught up with her and she ended up taking care of a baby, supposedly a prince of a nearby kingdom. This was how Sybel got tangled into affairs of other humans and this is how she discovered her own previously unknown emotions: love, hate, and everything in between. <br><br>I found myself in the situation when I need to say something nice about the book which totally deserves it, but I cannot find anything worth saying. My reviewing motto is, "When you want to praise a book and you have no idea what to say, praise the writing quality". Yes, the writing quality is great and on the level only few books of the genre can reach. The prose is excellent and so is the flow of the sentences. <br><br>What did not work for me was Sybel herself. For starters by the middle of the book <b>every</b> single named male character of the story was madly in love with her. I mean she was not exactly Helen of Troy whose face could launch a thousand ships. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532914694i/26048716.jpg" alt="Helen of Troy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She did not hesitate to sacrifice lives of people of several armies to get a personal revenge on one guy: can we call this an overkill? <br><br>Other than Sybel the only character showing any signs of being a living being was Coren. The rest were serving just to move the story along.<br><br>Lots of people love the book and my problem was that I was looking for great characters and could not find any that interest me. I already mentioned that the writing quality is very good. I should also mention interesting symbolism in the story that was mentioned by my buddy readers. <br><br>The final rating is the middle of the road: 3 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="900356290223739797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9819355479459473351">What made this novel really amazing is how excellent Patricia A. McKillip wrote this. The author used her skill to write majestic words to describe each character and places, as well as breathtaking prose to narrate the story. <br/><br/>If I'm not mistaken, this book was first published four decades ago and that it also won the World Fantasy Award for Novel in 1975.   <span id="freeText9819355479459473351" style="display:none">What made this novel really amazing is how excellent Patricia A. McKillip wrote this. The author used her skill to write majestic words to describe each character and places, as well as breathtaking prose to narrate the story. <br /><br />If I'm not mistaken, this book was first published four decades ago and that it also won the World Fantasy Award for Novel in 1975. It wouldn't be winning an award if it's not good, right? McKillip utilized her eloquence that made the story of Sybel, Tam, Coren, and of the beasts a truly astounding novel that everyone must read.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=my-shelf">my-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=mythopoeic-fiction">mythopoeic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782330005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3386600201669223244">This book gave me chills. Still does. <br/><br/>I went in knowing nothing about it. I mean, I did skim some of the reviews, so I knew it was highly rated and people seemed to love, but other than that, I had no idea what it's about or what to expect, and I had never read Patricia McKillip before.<br/><br/>And that was the best way to approach because the writing blew me away. It is simply SO GOOD and has a beautiful fluidity to it that makes it so easy to fall into. <br/><br/>What impresses me most is that the prose is neith</span>
  <span id="freeText3386600201669223244" style="display:none">This book gave me chills. Still does. <br /><br />I went in knowing nothing about it. I mean, I did skim some of the reviews, so I knew it was highly rated and people seemed to love, but other than that, I had no idea what it's about or what to expect, and I had never read Patricia McKillip before.<br /><br />And that was the best way to approach because the writing blew me away. It is simply SO GOOD and has a beautiful fluidity to it that makes it so easy to fall into. <br /><br />What impresses me most is that the prose is neither purple nor flowery; it's just lovely to read. There's a dreamy, poignant, lyrical quality to it, yet it's so easy to read and so concise. There's not an unnecessary scene or line or moment anywhere. Every word serves a purpose, and not once during the read did I feel like the story was wandering around aimlessly. Nothing is out of place, and so much happens in so few pages. And I just love that kind of writing--purposeful and minimalistic in execution. <br /><br />So what is this book about?<br /><br />Briefly: Sybel, a young powerful sorceress who knows nothing of the world below her mountain and wants nothing to do with it, is pushed into the affairs of two warring sides within a kingdom when a baby is brought to her to raise. <br /><br />On one side, there's an insecure king who fears being dethroned. On the other side, there's family of nobles who would like to dethrone the king. Their animosity toward each other go way back. Both sides want Sybel and use her powers for their own, but only one seeks out a way to break and bind her to their will. What follows is an all consuming tale of near destruction.<br /><br />Well... not exactly, but that was what it felt like during the read, like everything was coming apart at the seams, and I could not turn the page fast enough.<br /><br />Sometimes, after a string of bland genre picks, I would forget what it's like to read well written fantasy, but then something always comes along to remind me. McKillip was the perfect reminder.<br /><blockquote>"What, in years to come, will you have in your life but a silence that is meaningless, ancient names that are never spoken beyond these walls? Who will you laugh with, when Tam is grown? Who will you love? The Liralen? It is a dream. Beyond this mountain, there is a place for you among the living."</blockquote><br /><blockquote>"You can weave your life for so long--only so long, and then a thing in the world out of your control will tug at one vital thread and leave you patternless and subdued."</blockquote><br /><blockquote>"Be patient. It will soon be over."<br />"Soon is such a long word," she whispered.</blockquote><br /><br />Cross-posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2017/03/31/the-forgotten-beasts-of-eld-by-patricia-a-mckillip/">https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3386600201669223244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8170192191211150699">This is my favorite book of all time. If I had to pick a desert island book, it would be this one.<br/><br/>There is something about the way this book flows that is actually literary magic. It's about magic, and riddles, and all sort of other legendary things but it's like fractal mathematics: beautiful, impossible for an ordinary human to understand, and yet hypnotic. Just the opening paragraph is chilling, and thrilling, and all sort of other trilling llls in a row. I can't describe this book, because i</span>
  <span id="freeText8170192191211150699" style="display:none">This is my favorite book of all time. If I had to pick a desert island book, it would be this one.<br /><br />There is something about the way this book flows that is actually literary magic. It's about magic, and riddles, and all sort of other legendary things but it's like fractal mathematics: beautiful, impossible for an ordinary human to understand, and yet hypnotic. Just the opening paragraph is chilling, and thrilling, and all sort of other trilling llls in a row. I can't describe this book, because its better than that. It's not funny, or cute, or silly or any of those things. It's a work of pure lyrical genius. If you haven't read it yet, shame on you. </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015375126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7128384850210647229"><b>A dramatic, lyrical ballad locked into simple prose. Obscure, seemingly effortless, magical and breathtaking.</b> <br/><br/>I don't think I have ever come across a book like this before in the fantasy genre. <br/><br/>If I were to tell you what the story is about, it would not amount to much and there is hardly any worldbuilding, but the writing is so compelling, so powerful, so seductive and beautiful that I just cannot shake the effect it has had on me.<br/><br/>The music I kept hearing in my head while reading was the musical</span>
  <span id="freeText7128384850210647229" style="display:none"><b>A dramatic, lyrical ballad locked into simple prose. Obscure, seemingly effortless, magical and breathtaking.</b> <br><br>I don't think I have ever come across a book like this before in the fantasy genre. <br><br>If I were to tell you what the story is about, it would not amount to much and there is hardly any worldbuilding, but the writing is so compelling, so powerful, so seductive and beautiful that I just cannot shake the effect it has had on me.<br><br>The music I kept hearing in my head while reading was the musical suite, The Carnival of the Animals by Saint-Saëns, especially The Swan movement.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1505392490p8/3622243.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also there is a strong medieval feel to the whole story and I was very much reminded of the Arthurian myth by the relationship between Sybel, Coren and Drede. There was a strong Guinever-Lancelot-Arthur resemblance, though most of the time Sybel appeared to me as<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/724371.The_Lady_of_Shalott" title="The Lady of Shalott by Alfred Tennyson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lady of Shalott</a>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1505392567p8/3622247.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Arc received by the Publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</span>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Isa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1123165-hirondelle">Hirondelle</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196749117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9132614699670676527">One day <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25.Patricia_A__McKillip' title='Patricia A. McKillip' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patricia A. McKillip</a> will write a bad book and that'll be the first sign of the impending apocalypse. I have no idea how I went through so many years of my life without having read her books. Actually, that would probably be because there are no Portuguese translations and I have to buy the originals from the UK. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/81069.The_Forgotten_Beasts_of_Eld' title='The Forgotten Beasts of Eld by Patricia A. McKillip' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forgotten Beasts of Eld</a> is, in a word, <b>delightful</b>. Like all of McKillip's books the reader is lost in her magical worlds from the very first page. She writes things and they</span>
  <span id="freeText9132614699670676527" style="display:none">One day <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25.Patricia_A__McKillip" title="Patricia A. McKillip" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia A. McKillip</a> will write a bad book and that'll be the first sign of the impending apocalypse. I have no idea how I went through so many years of my life without having read her books. Actually, that would probably be because there are no Portuguese translations and I have to buy the originals from the UK. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/81069.The_Forgotten_Beasts_of_Eld" title="The Forgotten Beasts of Eld by Patricia A. McKillip" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forgotten Beasts of Eld</a> is, in a word, <b>delightful</b>. Like all of McKillip's books the reader is lost in her magical worlds from the very first page. She writes things and they seem to come alive, to leave the written paper and surround you, wherever you may be reading. <br /><br />Honestly, this book was so wonderful I was almost run over by a car while reading it and walking on the street. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9132614699670676527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2056630425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2056630425" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2056630425?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781616962777" href="/book/show/34724787-the-forgotten-beasts-of-eld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2056630425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16182547077081671957"><i>See this review and more like it on <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookbastion.net'>www.bookbastion.net</a></i><br/><br/>This year when I started book review blogging, I realized that I was reading an awful lot of brand new books that were garnering a lot of hype. Not that that's a bad thing, but I decided along the way that when the opportunity presented itself I also wanted to better acquaint myself with older books. <br/><br/><b>Stories that had been around for a lot longer are often written in a different way than the books of today.</b> There's less focus on continuous ac</span>
  <span id="freeText16182547077081671957" style="display:none"><i>See this review and more like it on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookbastion.net">www.bookbastion.net</a></i><br><br>This year when I started book review blogging, I realized that I was reading an awful lot of brand new books that were garnering a lot of hype. Not that that's a bad thing, but I decided along the way that when the opportunity presented itself I also wanted to better acquaint myself with older books. <br><br><b>Stories that had been around for a lot longer are often written in a different way than the books of today.</b> There's less focus on continuous action moving the plot, and in favor of more of a slow burn and lyrical prose. <br><br>In a lot of ways McKillip's writing style reminded me of Robin Hobb's <i>Assassin's Apprentice</i> which I also read earlier this year. <b>It's lofty and ambitious, and while the prose sometimes feels a little like it's meandering around descriptions and feelings, every word is purposefully chosen to deliver on the allegory of love and the unexpected places it takes a person.</b> Aside from the comparison to Hobb, there's also similarities shared with the old-style fairy tales, like the ones we might read as children. There are brief moments of darkness, but McKillip instead highlights all of the beauty and wonder of her world and it never stops feeling magical. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505600325ra/23939702.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I can't lie though, it certainly was a challenge at times. <b>McKillip doesn't serve every meaning to the reader on a silver platter. Instead, a lot is inferred during conversations or in the subtext.</b> I think this is the type of story that I could read a dozen times over and pick something new out of it each time. There are also a lot of references to places, people and events in the world that the reader never sees. It all serves to make the setting feel more open and lived in, and while it can be overwhelming, fans of the fantasy genre will find a lot to love there. <br><br><b>As a parable about love and loss, motherhood and letting go, it truly is a wonderful read.</b> A lot of fantasy novels become grounded in the fantastic. In the magical battles and swords and shields and plots for power. Those same topics are certainly brought up here, but they're touched upon in an ancillary sort of way as Mckillip chooses to ground her novel in very human struggles instead. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505600325ra/23939703.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>It was a lovely take on fantasy, and in a lot of ways the story still feels timeless in spite of having first been published in 1974. </b><br><br>A lovely and beautifully written story. <br><br><b>4 out of 5 stars</b><br><br><i>Thank you to Netgalley and Tachyon Publications for an ARC of this book!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16182547077081671957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1616443892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1616443892" />
    <a title="A. Dawes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55066255-a-dawes"><img alt="A. Dawes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470731545p2/55066255.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1616443892?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A. Dawes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A. Dawes" href="/user/show/55066255-a-dawes">A. Dawes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1616443892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8225064896140545253">Patricia A. Mckillip is one of my favourite fantasy writers. At the risk of sounding politically incorrect in a PC world, I find her voice uniquely feminine. Her prose is both rhythmical and intoxicating. <br/><br/>In this novel of isolation and seclusion, Sybil is brought up by her father on Eld mountain. Her sole companions are animals, which her father calls to the area. When Sybil's father passes away, isolated Sybil - still with only her beasts for company- studies magic to evolve into a powerful sor</span>
  <span id="freeText8225064896140545253" style="display:none">Patricia A. Mckillip is one of my favourite fantasy writers. At the risk of sounding politically incorrect in a PC world, I find her voice uniquely feminine. Her prose is both rhythmical and intoxicating. <br /><br />In this novel of isolation and seclusion, Sybil is brought up by her father on Eld mountain. Her sole companions are animals, which her father calls to the area. When Sybil's father passes away, isolated Sybil - still with only her beasts for company- studies magic to evolve into a powerful sorceress. Sybil expends much of her time trying to call-up a unique creature that might grant her more liberty, yet one day, a man called Coren arrives requesting that Sybil raises and protects a baby. Sybil is soon drawn into a conflict of the outside world of men, and the baby, Tam, matures. <br /><br />The novel explores isolation and individual growth through the love and friendship of others, along with the more darker traits of the human condition - the quest and rivalry for power. McKillip has a deft touch, and both the plot and her unique style of writing will make this a compelling read for most. It's targeted at a young adult audience but I personally feel as though adult readers will glean just as much, if not more, from this strong work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8225064896140545253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2124799355" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2124799355" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2124799355?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781616962777" href="/book/show/34724787-the-forgotten-beasts-of-eld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=review-freebie">review-freebie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2124799355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7004873746132242718">Originally reviewed at <a href='https://bookwraiths.com/2017/09/15/flashback-friday/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths</a>.<br/><br/><i>The Forgotten Beasts of Eld</i> is a wonderfully written, richly textured, high fantasy from Patricia A. McKillip. Even though it is quite limited in length, it is still filled with insightful moments and fascinating insights; all of it set in beautifully rendered fairy tale world.<br/><br/>Sybel is a young, powerful sorceress, who has spent her life in isolation, her interaction with humans nonexistent. She knows nothing outside of her mountain home, nor does she really wis</span>
  <span id="freeText7004873746132242718" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="https://bookwraiths.com/2017/09/15/flashback-friday/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths</a>.<br /><br /><i>The Forgotten Beasts of Eld</i> is a wonderfully written, richly textured, high fantasy from Patricia A. McKillip. Even though it is quite limited in length, it is still filled with insightful moments and fascinating insights; all of it set in beautifully rendered fairy tale world.<br /><br />Sybel is a young, powerful sorceress, who has spent her life in isolation, her interaction with humans nonexistent. She knows nothing outside of her mountain home, nor does she really wish to know. Her only companions the magical creatures of her home. So when a baby is brought to her she isn’t quite prepared for the emotions this innocent child will evoke — nor is she ready for the power struggle she will be brought into when someone returns for the child.<br /><br />What always catches me unprepared whenever I read (or reread) a Patricia A. McKillip novel is her unbelievable prose. It isn’t elaborate or flowery, merely lyrical and purposeful. Every word has its place and its use in her narratives, yet she never feels a need to expound unnecessarily. Important events taking place in pages rather than chapters. Concise, meaningful, and lovely. That is how this author writes, and I only wish more fantasy offerings these days mimicked her style.<br /><br />As for the story itself, it was poignant, quick, and emotional. Sybel’s life, her choices, and the ones she love caught up in the quagmire she has unknowingly been drawn into. Her words and response to both the child and that which comes later filled with a layer of meaning and depth which will truly touches a reader’s heart strings.<br /><br />As for any criticisms or complaints, I have none. McKillip has always been a writer I was in awe of, especially her amazing ability to craft an exciting fantasy tale that still finds a place for both dignity and seriousness in its pages, and <i>The Enchanted Beasts of Eld</i> was no exception, making me wonder only why it took me so long to actually read it.<br /><br />Lyrical, complex, concise, and emotional, this novel is one I will be readily espousing to lovers of high fantasy, fairy tales, and beautifully writing. Patricia A. McKillip isn’t an author spoken of very often these days, but she should be, because her works are treasures of the genre.<br /><br />I received this book from the publisher in exchange for a fair and honest review. I’d like to thank them for allowing me to receive this review copy and inform everyone that the review you have read is my opinion alone.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2132440224" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2132440224" />
    <a title="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks"><img alt="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592760668p2/13716524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2132440224?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" href="/user/show/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks">Evelina | AvalinahsBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781616962777" href="/book/show/34724787-the-forgotten-beasts-of-eld">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=arcs-or-review-copies">arcs-or-review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=owned-ebooks-read">owned-ebooks-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=books-of-2017">books-of-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=short-reads">short-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2132440224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15856918063558112722">I both liked and disliked this book... Took me ages to get invested in it (about half the book...), but then it got interesting. I feel like it's because midway, the book changes quite drastically. It starts involving FEELINGS. Love, revenge. Before that? I knew as much as you do what was going on.<br/><br/>There are reasons why I dislike high fantasy (or at least high-ish) fantasy, but I still keep trying... I should stop. I am not comfortable with a crucial thing most high fantasies do, and that's dropp</span>
  <span id="freeText15856918063558112722" style="display:none">I both liked and disliked this book... Took me ages to get invested in it (about half the book...), but then it got interesting. I feel like it's because midway, the book changes quite drastically. It starts involving FEELINGS. Love, revenge. Before that? I knew as much as you do what was going on.<br /><br />There are reasons why I dislike high fantasy (or at least high-ish) fantasy, but I still keep trying... I should stop. I am not comfortable with a crucial thing most high fantasies do, and that's dropping 50 inconsequential names of legendary kings and beasts on me in the first page, none of which pretty much relate to the story at all, are described or are even to do with mythology - so basically, I end up with a jumble of interesting sounding syllables that mean nothing to me. Am I weird? This was a big problem for me with this book, and a reason I found to get it hard to get into at first.<br /><br />But that isn't the only reason this book didn't hook first. The storytelling is basically like a fairytale. In one sentence they talk about a thing, in the next sentence, it's suddenly twelve years later and the thing has been done. A baby basically left at the doorstep suddenly becomes dearer than anyone the characters known before. People love each other although they've talked three times and disliked each other during those dialogues. They meet kings and talk with them as of they've always known them... Granted, it does give a fairytale vibe, but I do not enjoy this kind of storytelling because it's incredibly jumpy, and it also feels quite terribly unnatural. I had trouble paying attention.<br /><br />But when it gets past that point, I must admit it does get interesting, and quite dark. And meaningful. If this book was like this in its entirety, I would have surely given it 4 stars! But I almost dropped it at 38%. So 3 stars it is. But if you like high fantasy, I'm sure you'll like this!<br /><br /><a href="http://avalinahsbooks.space/?utm_source=goodreads&amp;utm_medium=review&amp;utm_campaign=The%20Forgotten%20Beasts%20of%20Eld" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/avalinahsbooks/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">My Bookstagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/AvalinahsBooks" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookish Twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15856918063558112722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_2132440224'><a id="like_count_review_2132440224" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/2132440224?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">28 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F81069.The_Forgotten_Beasts_of_Eld">Like</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1367000241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367000241" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487528389p2/11475773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1367000241?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1367000241&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367000241" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12886750081156387531"><br/><i>“The giant Grof was hit in one eye by a stone, and that eye turned inward so that it looked into his mind and he died of what he saw there.”</i><br/><br/>The Forgotten Beasts of Eld was written by Patricia McKillip and published in 1974. It won the 1975 World Fantasy Award. Spoilers follow, as well as as a discussion of sexual violence.<br/><br/><b>So What's It About?</b><br/><br/>The young sorceress Sybel lives alone on her mountain, surrounded by the marvelous, ancient beasts of legend that her father called to him. She is content to</span>
  <span id="freeText12886750081156387531" style="display:none"><br /><i>“The giant Grof was hit in one eye by a stone, and that eye turned inward so that it looked into his mind and he died of what he saw there.”</i><br /><br />The Forgotten Beasts of Eld was written by Patricia McKillip and published in 1974. It won the 1975 World Fantasy Award. Spoilers follow, as well as as a discussion of sexual violence.<br /><br /><b>So What's It About?</b><br /><br />The young sorceress Sybel lives alone on her mountain, surrounded by the marvelous, ancient beasts of legend that her father called to him. She is content to tend to the animals and gather secrets, but one night a strange young man comes to the mountain with a baby in his arms. The baby is a relation of Sybel's, born to the Queen of Drede and her lover. Sybel knows nothing of love but she takes the baby in, drawing her into the treacherous world of human power and emotion for the first time.<br /><br /><b>What I Thought</b><br /><br />I really wish I had a sufficient grasp of the English language to tell you how Patricia McKillip's writing makes me feel. In my opinion there are few fantasy authors who have as perfect a command of the written word. She is poetic without becoming overwrought, thoughtful without becoming ponderous, ethereal without becoming detached from the humanity of her characters. Each one of her novels is a perfect little dreamscape, an exquisitely-wrought fairy tale that unfolds before you one lush sentence at a time.<br /><br />The Forgotten Beasts of Eld is in many ways concerned with what it means to exist with others in the word. Sybel is constantly torn between isolating herself on her mountain and descending into the world of men: one way lies certainty and safety but loneliness and emptiness, the other way lies all of the joy and terrifying pain that comes from vulnerability. When she is hurt in the deepest way after venturing into the world of men, the book also considers the question of what Sybel owes the world in return for the ways that it has both wronged her and provided her with joy- does she owe it her rage and vengeance, or her continued love and vulnerability?<br /><br />I think the book is at its most powerful when it meditates on love and hate, and how we change based not only how we love and hate, but on how we act based on these emotions. At the start of the book Sybel tells Coren that she does "not understand loving and hating, only being and knowing." She is skittish and cold, slow to trust and deeply leery of others, but gradually comes to know what it truly means to care for others as she is drawn into the world with Coren, Tam and the mountain witch Maegla. Her relationship with Coren is at the heart of her struggle between isolation and trust:<br /><br /><i>"What do you think love is—a thing to startle from the heart like a bird at every shout or blow? You can fly from me, high as you choose into your darkness, but you will see me always beneath you, no matter how far away, with my face turned to you. My heart is in your heart. I gave it to you with my name that night and you are its guardian, to treasure it, or let it wither and die."</i><br /><br />Sybel learns to hate when the King of Drede, in his obsession with her, hires a sorcerer to strip away her willpower so she will belong to him without any question of a struggle. The sorcerer, Mithran, decides that he will keep Sybel for himself instead, and she is paralyzed as he begins to assault her. After killing him and escaping, Sybel's hatred for the king grows and consumes her:<br /><br /><i>"How did you hate? Did you nurse revenge from a tiny, moon-pale seedling in the night places in your heart, watch it grow and flower and bear dark fruit that hung ripe—ripe for the plucking? It becomes a great, twisted thing of dark leaves and thick, winding vines that chokes and withers whatever good things grow in your heart; it feeds on all the hatred your heart can bear—That is what is in me, Coren. Not all the wondrous joy and love of you can wither that night plant in me."</i><br /><br />She embraces all of the coldness that she once harbored for the world and hatches a plot that will strip Drede of all of his power and leave him helpless and terrified just as he tried to do with her. It is a plot that involves war, manipulation and deceiving Coren while strategizing with his violence-mongering brothers. Ultimately, she realizes that she must confront the mass of hatred and love that has grown inside of her. I want to return to this thought after considering the attack on Sybel in a little more depth.<br /><br /><b>The F Word</b><br /><br />Drede and Mithran both attempt to strip Sybel of all agency and control her utterly. Their violence towards her is at its heart a matter of men being afraid of a woman's power: in this case her literal magical power and knowledge, but also her ability to consent or not, to reject them think independently for herself and find them wanting. They cannot experience love or desire outside a context of complete control because of this fear; they cannot experience admiration for Sybel without this terror that she will be more powerful than them. In some ways I think this is another meditation on vulnerability; this time, the way that our constructions of masculinity perpetuate violence towards women through their destruction of vulnerability:<br /><br /><i>“Sybel, I am helpless in this matter. I want you, but I am afraid of you..."</i><br /><br />After their attacks on her, Sybel's story becomes one of all-consuming rage as a result of victimization. It's common to hear that there is no wrong emotional response to experiencing trauma, and the core message here is very much in line with this. But what I think McKillip is concerned with goes beyond what one feels and extends to what one does in response to trauma. Sybel's ultimate realization is that she has every right to feel hatred and anger in response to what was done to her, but she has hurt those she loves by deceiving and manipulating them, plotting for a war that would destroy their lives and manipulating Coren's mind just as Mithran would have done to her. In the process she has also damaged herself:<br /><br /><i>“But you had a right to be angry.”<br />“Yes. But not to hurt those I love, or myself."</i><br /><br />It's the story of a marvelous, strange young woman and the tremendous power that she wields, it's the story of her ancient beasts and their secrets, it's the story of love that survives great wrongs, and it is ultimately the story of Sybel starting to heal:<br /><br /><i>"Come with me tomorrow through the forest; we will gather black mushrooms and herbs that, crushed against the fingers, give a magic smell. You will feel the sun on your hair and the rich earth beneath your feet, and the fresh winds scented with the spice of snow from the hidden places on Eld Mountain. Be patient, as you must always be patient with new pale seeds buried in the dark ground. When you are stronger, you can begin to think again. But now is the time to feel.”</i><br /><br /><b>About the Author</b><br /><br />Patricia McKillip was born in 1948 and grew up in Oregon, Britain and Germany. She received her bachelors and masters degrees in English from San Jose State University. She briefly considered becoming a classical pianist before becoming an author; her first book was The House on Parchment Street, published in 1973. The Forgotten Beasts of Eld won her the World Fantasy Award in 1975, and she is perhaps best known for the Riddlemaster trilogy, starting with The Riddlemaster of Hed. She lives in Bend, Oregon with her husband, poet David Lunde.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12886750081156387531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2124149978" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2124149978" />
    <a title="Sheila Goicea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33749824-sheila-goicea"><img alt="Sheila Goicea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581698225p2/33749824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2124149978?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheila Goicea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheila Goicea" href="/user/show/33749824-sheila-goicea">Sheila Goicea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34330548-the-forgotten-beasts-of-eld">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who loved Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them by J.K. Rowling</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=color-me-with-this-cover">color-me-with-this-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=fantasy-young-adult">fantasy-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=arc-ebook">arc-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=includes-dragons">includes-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=includes-magic">includes-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=arc-via-netgalley">arc-via-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=2017-completed-reads">2017-completed-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=2017-releases">2017-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33749824-sheila-goicea?shelf=2017-top-picks">2017-top-picks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2124149978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16214288130571383500">See my full review of this book on my blog along with others at: <a href='https://foalsfictionandfiligree.com/the-forgotten-beasts-of-eld/' rel='nofollow noopener'>foalsfictionandfiligree.com</a>.<br/><br/><i>I received an ARC of this book from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!</i> <i>All included quotes have been taken from an ARC and may not match the finished publication.</i> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551373113i/27131473._SY540_.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Released today!</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“I need you to forgive me. And then perhaps I can begin to forgive myself. There is no one but you who can do that either.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>A book like this is <i>intimidating</i> to pick up. Not because it is mundane, nor becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText16214288130571383500" style="display:none">See my full review of this book on my blog along with others at: <a href="https://foalsfictionandfiligree.com/the-forgotten-beasts-of-eld/" rel="nofollow noopener">foalsfictionandfiligree.com</a>.<br><br><i>I received an ARC of this book from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!</i> <i>All included quotes have been taken from an ARC and may not match the finished publication.</i> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551373113i/27131473._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Released today!</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I need you to forgive me. And then perhaps I can begin to forgive myself. There is no one but you who can do that either.”</i>
</blockquote><br>A book like this is <i>intimidating</i> to pick up. Not because it is mundane, nor because it is necessarily daunting (although it is, in a way). No, my friends. This book entails every aspect that fantasy writing is about, and it is truly <b>breathtaking.</b> Being disappointed with other fantasy reads after this book is why it is intimidating. <br><br>Compared to the writing of today's YA novels, this book automatically takes the lead in its overall quality. Its writing style, detail to plot and meaningfulness are (in my opinion) <b>so much more</b> when compared to what is out there today.<br><br>We are dropped into a new world, that isn't ever fully explained. Because of this, the reader is <b>allowed to be left with a sense of yearning and wonderment to know <i>more</i></b>. To me, this is the key element to draw in the reader, and to make them thirst for <i>more</i>. Over-explanation of detail only "dumbs down" the writing to be taken at face-value, rather than allowing the readers' imagination to run wild. The tidbits that we are privy to are delicious, whimsical, and <b>truly meaningful</b>.<br><br><b>Now, to the story...</b><br><br>Our main character Sybel, is the daughter of Ogam, a man born from a line of wizards. His special powers allowed him to "call" many spectacular creatures to live among his castle walls, safely nestled in the mountains of Eld. Sybel, growing up in a world separate from the one she lives in, knows little of the outside world. She cares little for the dealings of men, and spends her time tending her beloved creatures, and calling the fabled Lorien, a mythical white bird, to join her. <br><br>Her solitude is interrupted when an unbidden man brings a baby to her doorsteps, insisting that she takes the child in and raises him in a place far away from the warring nations outside her walls. She consents, and realizes that she must learn what it means to love another human--something she is not used to doing. <br><br>As the child grows into a young man, Sybel develops a strong, motherly connection to him. But as he comes of age, Tamlorn is sought out, and called to rejoin the world of men, and take his rightful place as prince. Sybel calls Tamlorn's father, the king Drede to her to discuss terms for Tamlorn. When Drede meets Sybel, he immediately falls in love with her, and extends the offer for her to join him and Tamlorn. <br><br>Because of Sybel's odd upbringing and talents, she has developed a rather cold character. She doesn't know, or care much for the toils of men. That is, until she discovers that she is <i>used</i> by one who desires her for her power. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“It is not a bad thing, itself, but it is a bad thing to be used by men, to have them choose what you must be, and what you must not be, to have little choice in your life.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Sybel's outlook on mankind transforms into a dark and corrupting thing,  causing her to unabashedly use others to cast her revenge. But her desires for revenge do not come without their consequences. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“The giant Grof was hit in one eye by a stone, and that eye turned inward so that it looked into his mind and he died of what he saw there.”</i>
</blockquote><br>As Sybel experiences life, love, loss, and joy, she must either grow, or forever be locked in the dark shackles of revenge, hurt, and mistrust. Because her character basically starts from zero, the reader gets to watch her "transform" as she learns more about human nature. <br><br><b>There are two different points in this book that I didn't necessarily like, and made me take a half-star off:</b><br><br><b>#1</b> Because this is a shorter novel, changes aren't always allowed enough time to happen without feeling a bit forced. An example of this is Sybel's character. She changes so much in such a short amount of time, that it isn't always believable.<br><br><b>#2</b> I felt that the imaginative expression could be slightly overwhelming at times, and could have used a <i>bit</i> more explanation. <br><br>Despite these two things, it is without a doubt that this is a beautiful story of growth, hardship, healing, and forgiveness. I would highly recommend this read to any lover of young adult fantasy.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551373113ra/27131472.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Random side note: I think that <i>Sybel</i> is the original white-haired, dragon wielding heroine. Not Khaleesi</i>.<br><br><b>Vulgarity:</b> None that I recall.<br><b>Sexual content:</b> Some advances are made towards Sybel, but they are stopped before anything happens.<br><b>Violence:</b> Minimal. <br><br><b>My Rating:</b> ★★★★1/2<br><br><a href="http://foalsfictionandfiligree.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ¦ <a href="https://instagram.com/foalsfictionandfiligree/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookstagram</a> ¦ <a href="https://twitter.com/shesgoinbookcrz" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ¦ <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/foalsfictionandfiligree/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> ¦ <a href="https://www.facebook.com/foalsfictionandfiligree/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16214288130571383500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer18371106620275125200">Somehow I have managed to live my life without reading this masterpiece of high fantasy. Somehow....<br/><br/>Now that I have I wish I can time travel to 5 days ago when I haven't read it and read it again for the first time.<br/>Isn't that always the wish when we read a book that moves us?<br/><br/><blockquote>"I do not want to choose which one of you I must love or hate.   <span id="freeText18371106620275125200" style="display:none">Somehow I have managed to live my life without reading this masterpiece of high fantasy. Somehow....<br /><br />Now that I have I wish I can time travel to 5 days ago when I haven't read it and read it again for the first time.<br />Isn't that always the wish when we read a book that moves us?<br /><br /><blockquote>"I do not want to choose which one of you I must love or hate. Here, I am free to do neither. I want no part of your bitterness."</blockquote><br /><br />The prose was simple, yet so amazingly lyrical. The language used was evocative, emotional. This is a beautifully written book.<br /><br /><blockquote>"You can weave your life so long— only so long, and then a thing in the world out of your control will tug at one vital thread and leave you patternless and subdued.”</blockquote><br /><br />Coren was my absolute hero!!!! He was brave and valorous and honorable and strong and kind-hearted and understanding... and a ginger!! What more can a girl ask for??<br /><br /><blockquote>"I heard you. Sometimes, in silence, at night, I hear the voices of things beyond eyesight, like echoes of ancient songs. I heard your voice, lonely in my dreams—it woke me, so I came. You see, I know how it is when you speak a name into an empty room with no one on earth to answer to it."“</blockquote><br /><br />Sybel at times frustrated me when she wanted to go at the world (the king) alone, or at least without Coren's help. Fearing what he would think of her. But even when he found everything out by accident, this is what he says:<br /><br /><blockquote>"What do you think love is—a thing to startle from the heart like a bird at every shout or blow? You can fly from me, high as you choose into your darkness, but you will see me always beneath you, no matter how far away, with my face turned to you. My heart is in your heart. “</blockquote><br /><br />I read this for book club and can anyone guess how excited I am for the discussion?????</span>

<div id="review_1149150880" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149150880" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1149150880?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149150880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9979777643183882414">Somehow, from the midst of feeling dreadful because of this cold, I realised that what I really wanted to read was something by Patricia McKillip. It’s so strange how I disliked the first book of hers I read; I feel like I appreciate her work more with each book I do read. And this one… it’s fairytale-like, mythic — a review on GR said ‘parable like’, and yes: that too. It’s full of epic fantasy elements but the real struggle is between taking revenge and being true to who you really are and tho</span>
  <span id="freeText9979777643183882414" style="display:none">Somehow, from the midst of feeling dreadful because of this cold, I realised that what I really wanted to read was something by Patricia McKillip. It’s so strange how I disliked the first book of hers I read; I feel like I appreciate her work more with each book I do read. And this one… it’s fairytale-like, mythic — a review on GR said ‘parable like’, and yes: that too. It’s full of epic fantasy elements but the real struggle is between taking revenge and being true to who you really are and those you love. (The phrase “being true to yourself” sounds annoyingly cliché, but I can’t think of another way to put that without quoting the whole book.)<br /><br />McKillip’s writing is gorgeous, and works well with the character she’s chosen — a girl who has not been loved, does not know how to love; who hasn’t been among people to be drawn into loves and hatreds. And in the course of the book she does learn, and she struggles with it… There’s a coolness to the book, like a mountain stream; an aloofness that you can get with distance from something, but toward everything. I can understand why some people disliked it for that very thing, but for me it perfectly matched the subject.<br /><br />I like high fantasy, but since so much of it draws from the same well as Tolkien, there’s something all too real about it sometimes. This book, the character of Sybel, are closer to real magic for me, in the same way that the contemplative parts of Ursula Le Guin’s Earthsea books (the sleeping man with the thistle growing by his hand…) come closer to real magic for me than all the magic rings and restless shades in the world.<br /><br />And one last thing to love: I adore the way that the relationship between Coren and Sybel works out. That it has to be worked on, from both sides, that it’s not always matched.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9979777643183882414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
